Wife Chooses Herself: One Ba'in Divorce
Ruling and proof for one ba'in divorce when wife chooses herself

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a wife chooses herself after 'ikhtari' and explain the role of istihsan based on ijma overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
When a wife chooses herself after 'ikhtari', only one ba'in divorce occurs by istihsan overriding qiyas.

This lesson examines a distinctive Hanafi ruling where the husband delegates the power of divorce to his wife using the word 'ikhtari' (choose). Upon her choosing herself, a single irrevocable divorce takes effect. The passage reveals how the Hanafi school prioritizes the consensus of the Companions over strict analogy (qiyas) and explains why the wife's choice cannot produce three divorces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the wife's response 'I choose myself' after the husband says 'ikhtari'. The ruling is that one ba'in (irrevocable) divorce occurs.
Ba'in means the marriage ends immediately; reconciliation requires a new marriage contract.
2
Understand the qiyas counter-argument
Qiyas (analogy) would dictate that no divorce occurs because the husband himself cannot effect divorce with the word 'ikhtari', so he cannot delegate that power to another.
This shows the tension between textual evidence and analogical reasoning.
3
Locate the Hanafi proof: istihsan based on ijma
The Hanafi school adopts istihsan (juristic preference) due to the consensus (ijma) of the Companions, which validates the delegation. The husband's authority over the marriage also supports this.
Ijma is a primary source of law; here it overrides qiyas.
4
Examine the indivisibility of ikhtiyar
The wife's act of choosing herself is a single, indivisible act. Therefore, even if the husband intended three divorces, only one occurs. This contrasts with the phrase 'anti ba'in' where baynunah can be divided into degrees.
The ruling prevents the intention from multiplying the number of divorces.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اختاری کے جواب میں عورت نے نفس کو اختیار کرلیا تو ایک طلاق بائنہ واقع ہو جائے گی
فان اختارت نفسها في قوله اختارى كانت واحدة بائنة والقياس ان لا يقع بهذا شيء وان نوى الزوج الطلاق لانه لايملك الايقاع بهذا اللفظ فلايملك التفويض الى غيره الا انا استحسناه لاجماع الصحابة رضى الله عنهم ولانه بسبيل من ان يستديم نكا حها اويفارقها فیملک اقامتها مقام نفسه في حق هذا الحكم ثم الواقع بها بائن لان اختيارها نفسها بثبوت اختصاصنا بها وذلك فى البائن ولا يكون ثلثا وان نوى الزوج ذلك لأن الاختيار لايتنوع بخلاف الابانة لان البينونة قد تتنوع
ترجمہ ... پس اگر اس عورت نے اپنے آپ کو اختیار کیا اس کے قول لفظ اختیاری کی صورت میں تو ایک بائنہ ہوگی ۔ اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ اس سے کچھ واقع نہ ہو۔ اگر چہ شوہر نے طلاق کی نیت کی ہو۔ کیونکہ شوہر اس لفظ سے واقع کرنے کا مالک نہیں ہے۔ پس اپنے علاوہ کی طرف بھی سپرد کرنے کا مالک نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن ہم نے اس کو استحسانا جائز جانا ہے۔ صحابہ کے اجماع کی وجہ سے۔ اور اسلئے کہ شوہر کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ وہ اسکے نکاح کو برابر قائم رکھے۔ یا اسکو جدا کر دے۔ پس شوہر اس عورت کو اپنا قائم مقام بنانے کا مالک ہو گا اس حکم میں ۔ پھر اس سے بائنہ ہی واقع ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اس عورت کا اپنے آپ کو اختیار کرنا نفس کے ساتھ عورت کے اختصاص کو ثابت کرنے کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اور یہ بات بائن میں ہوگی۔ اور تین نہیں ہوں گی۔ اگر چہ شوہر نے اس کی نیت کی ہو۔ کیونکہ اختیار منقسم نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ بخلاف ابانت کے۔ اسلئے کہ بینونت منقسم ہوتی ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ شوہر کے لفظ اختیاری کہنے کے بعد اگر عورت نے اسی مجلس میں اپنے نفس کو اختیار کر لیا تو یہ ایک طلاق سے بائنہ ہوگی۔ یہی قول حضرت علی کا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ اس لفظ سے کوئی طلاق واقع نہ ہو۔ اگر چہ شوہر نے طلاق کی نیت کی ہو۔ کیونکہ شوہر اس لفظ سے خود طلاق واقع کرنے کا مالک نہیں ہے۔ لہذا دوسرے کو مالک بنانے کا کیسے مالک ہوگا۔ مگر صحابہ کے اجماع کی وجہ سے اس کو استحسانا جائز قرار دے دیا ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر کو یہ اختیار حاصل ہے کہ وہ اپنی بیوی کے نکاح کو قائم رکھے یا اس کو جدا کر دے۔ پس وہ اس اختیار میں اپنی بیوی کو اپنا قائم مقام بھی بنا سکتا ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس لفظ اختیاری سے ایک بائنہ واقع ہوگی کیونکہ عورت کا اپنے نفس کو اختیار کرنا اس وقت ثابت ہوگا جبکہ نفس کے ساتھ عورت کا اختصاص ثابت ہو جائے یعنی شوہر کی ملک زائل ہو جائے اور عورت اپنے نفس کی مالک ہو جائے اور ظاہر ہے کہ یہ بات طلاق بائن میں حاصل ہوگی۔ اور اگر شوہر نے تین طلاقوں کی نیت کی تو تین واقع نہیں ہوں گی۔ کیونکہ اختیار منقسم نہیں ہوتا۔ البتہ بینونت غلیظہ اور خفیفہ کی طرف منقسم ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس وجہ سے انت بائن میں تین طلاقوں کی نیت درست ہے۔ مگر اختیار کی صورت میں تین کی نیت صحیح نہیں ہے۔
If the wife chooses herself in response to his saying 'ikhtari', then one ba'in divorce occurs. And qiyas (analogy) is that nothing would occur even if the husband intended divorce, because he is not the owner of effecting divorce with this word, so he is not the owner of delegating to someone else. But we deem it permissible by istihsan due to the ijma of the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) and because he has the way to either continue her marriage or separate from her, so he has the ability to place her in his own position with respect to this ruling. Then that which occurs is ba'in because her choosing herself is due to establishing her own exclusive right over herself, and that is in ba'in divorce. And it will not become three even if the husband intended that, because choice (ikhtiyar) is not divisible, unlike baynunah (separateness) because separateness is divisible. Translation: ... So if that woman chose herself in his saying 'ikhtari', then one ba'in divorce occurs. And qiyas is that nothing would occur even if the husband intended divorce, because the husband is not the owner of effecting divorce with this word, so he will not be the owner of entrusting it to someone else. But we have considered it permissible by istihsan due to the ijma of the Companions, and because the husband has the option to either keep her marriage intact or separate her. Therefore, the husband can make her his deputy in this ruling. Then only ba'in occurs because the woman's choosing herself is due to establishing her specific right over herself, and that is in ba'in divorce. And it will not be three even if the husband intended that, because choice is not divisible, unlike baynunah because separateness can be divided. Explanation of the issue: After the husband says the word 'ikhtari', if the wife chooses herself in the same session, then this is one ba'in divorce. This is also the saying of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him). The author of Hidayah says that qiyas requires that no divorce occurs with this word, even if the husband intended divorce, because the husband is not the owner of effecting divorce with this word himself, so how can he make someone else the owner? But due to the ijma of the Companions, this is deemed permissible by istihsan. A second proof is that the husband has the option to either keep his wife's marriage intact or separate her, so he can also make his wife his deputy in this option. The author of Hidayah says that from this word 'ikhtari', one ba'in divorce occurs because the wife's choosing herself is established only when her exclusive right over herself is established, i.e., the husband's ownership is removed and she becomes the owner of herself, and it is obvious that this occurs in ba'in divorce. And if the husband intended three divorces, three will not occur because choice is not divisible. However, baynunat (separateness) is divided into severe and light, so in 'anti ba'in', intending three divorces is valid, but in the case of ikhtiyar, intending three is not correct.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the wife's response of choosing herself when the husband says 'ikhtari'. The ruling is that one ba'in (irrevocable) divorce occurs. The passage then presents the qiyas (analogy) argument which would lead to no divorce at all, because the husband does not own the power to effect divorce with the word 'ikhtari' himself, so he cannot delegate it. However, the Hanafi school adopts istihsan (juristic preference) based on the ijma (consensus) of the Companions, which validates the delegation. A secondary proof is that the husband has the authority to continue or end the marriage, so he can appoint his wife as his deputy. The passage then explains that the divorce is ba'in because the wife's choice of herself implies her exclusive ownership of herself, which only occurs after the husband's marital authority is removed. Moreover, only one ba'in divorce occurs regardless of the husband's intention for three, because ikhtiyar (choice) is indivisible—it is a single act of selection. This contrasts with the phrase 'anti ba'in' (you are separate), where baynunah can be graded into minor and major separation. Thus, in 'ikhtari', the husband's intention of three does not effect three divorces.

Key Terms
اختارت نفسها (ikhtarat nafsaha): The wife says 'I choose myself,' which the text rules as one ba'in divorce.
بائنہ (ba'inah): An irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) that ends the marriage immediately without possibility of revocation, though remarriage is possible with a new contract.
اختیار (ikhtiyar): Choice; in this context, the act of the wife choosing herself, which is indivisible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the husband says 'ikhtari' intending three divorces, and the wife says 'I choose myself,' how many divorces occur?
A) Three divorces, because the husband intended them.
B) No divorce, because the husband cannot delegate.
C) One ba'in divorce, because choice is indivisible.
D) One raj'i divorce, because the wife's choice is a revocation.

Key Takeaway
When a wife chooses herself after her husband says 'ikhtari', only one ba'in divorce occurs, irrespective of the husband's intention, because ikhtiyar is indivisible and the ruling is established by istihsan over qiyas.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Necessity of Mentioning 'Nafs' in Ikhtiyar
Ruling that the word 'nafs' must appear in speech of either spouse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for talaq via ikhtiyar and explain why omitting 'nafs' invalidates the divorce.

Core Idea
A divorce via ikhtiyar requires explicit mention of 'nafs' — ambiguity cannot remove ambiguity.

In Hanafi divorce law, when a husband gives his wife the option of divorce (ikhtiyar), the word 'nafs' (self) must appear in the speech of either spouse. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof from ijma, and the linguistic principle that an ambiguous word cannot interpret another ambiguous term.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the pronouncement of ikhtiyar (giving choice) by the husband and the wife's response. The ruling states that if 'nafs' is not mentioned in either spouse's speech, the attempted divorce is invalid (batil).
The ruling applies specifically to talaq via ikhtiyar, not to other forms of divorce.
2
Locate the dalil (ijma)
The passage cites ijma (consensus) of the Companions as proof that 'nafs' must be mentioned. This is a qat'i (definitive) dalil.
Ijma is a primary source of law in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the reason: mubham cannot interpret mubham
The words 'ikhtari' (choose) and 'ikhtartu' (I chose) are both ambiguous (mubham). An ambiguous word cannot serve as an interpretation (tafsir) of another ambiguous word; specification requires a clear term like 'nafs'.
This is a usul principle: al-mubham la yufassiru al-mubham.
4
Apply the rule to the example
If the husband says 'ikhtari' and the wife says 'ikhtartu' (without 'nafsi'), no divorce occurs. But if the wife says 'ikhtartu nafsi' or 'talaqtuhu', the divorce is valid.
Substitutes for 'nafs' include 'ikhtartu nafsi' or 'talaqtuhu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لفظ نفس زوجین میں سے کسی ایک کی کلام میں ہونا ضروری ہے
قال ولابد من ذكر النفس فى كلامه او فى كلامها حتى لو قال لها اختارى فقالت قد اخترت فهو باطل لانه عرف بالاجماع وهو فى المفسر من احد الجانبين ولان المبهم لا يصلح تفسيرا للمبهم ولا تعين مع الابهام
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور نفس کا ذکر ضروری ہے شوہر کے کلام میں یا عورت کے کلام میں حتی کہ اگر عورت سے کہا اختیاری۔ پھر عورت نے کہا اخترت تو یہ باطل ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ اجماع سے معلوم ہوا ہے اور اجماع اس میں ہے کہ احد الجانبین میں تفسیر کی گئی ہو اور اسلئے کہ مبہم مبہم کی تفسیر بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا ہے۔ اور ابہام کے ساتھ تعین نہیں ہوتی ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ لفظ اختیار سے طلاق واقع کرنے کیلئے زوجین میں سے کسی ایک کے کلام میں لفظ نفس یا اسکے قائم مقام کا مذکور ہونا ضروری ہے ( نفس کا قائم مقام لفظ اختیارۃ اور تطلیقہ ہے ) چنانچہ اگر شوہر نے اختاری کہا اور عورت نے جواب میں اخترت کہہ دیا تو طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ اختیار سے طلاق کا واقع ہونا صحابہ کے اجماع سے ثابت ہے۔ اور صحابہ کا اجماع اس صورت میں
It is necessary that the word 'nafs' be in the speech of one of the spouses. He said: And it is necessary to mention 'nafs' in his speech or in her speech, so much so that if he said to her 'ikhtari' and she said 'ikhtartu' (I chose), then it is invalid because it is known by ijma, and it is that interpretation is made from one of the two sides, and because the ambiguous (mubham) is not fit to interpret the ambiguous, and determination does not occur with ambiguity. Translation: Quduri said: And mentioning 'nafs' is necessary in the husband's speech or in the wife's speech, so much so that if he said to her 'ikhtari', then she said 'ikhtartu', this is invalid because this is known from ijma, and the ijma is that interpretation is done from one of the two sides, and because the ambiguous cannot be an interpretation of the ambiguous, and determination does not occur with ambiguity. Explanation of the issue: For effecting divorce with the word 'ikhtiar', it is necessary that the word 'nafs' or its substitute be mentioned in the speech of one of the spouses (the substitute for 'nafs' is the word 'ikhtari' and 'tatliqah'). So if the husband said 'ikhtari' and the wife responded with 'ikhtartu', divorce will not occur. The proof is that the occurrence of divorce with the word 'ikhtiar' is established by the ijma of the Companions, and the ijma of the Companions is in this case...
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about the necessity of mentioning the word 'nafs' (self) or its equivalent in the speech of either the husband or the wife for divorce to take effect through ikhtiyar. The matn from Al-Hidayah (quoting Al-Quduri) states that it is required that 'nafs' be mentioned in either spouse's utterance. For instance, if the husband says 'ikhtari' (choose) and the wife merely says 'ikhtartu' (I chose) without saying 'nafsi' (myself), the divorce is invalid. The reason given is twofold: first, it is known by ijma (consensus) that the interpretation (of ikhtiyar as divorce) must come from one of the two sides—meaning one of them must specify the self; second, an ambiguous word (mubham) like 'ikhtartu' cannot serve as an interpretation of another ambiguous word ('ikhtari'). Determination (ta'yin) of the intended meaning cannot occur with ambiguity. The commentary further explains that substitutes for 'nafs' include saying 'ikhtartu nafsi' or 'ttalaqtuhu' (I divorce him). Thus, if the wife says 'ikhtartu' without specifying herself, no divorce occurs. The proof from ijma is that the Companions agreed that talaq through ikhtiyar only happens when the self is specified, as in the well-known incident of the wives of the Prophet choosing Allah and His Messenger.

Key Terms
نفس (nafs): The word 'self' which must be mentioned in the speech of either spouse for talaq to take effect via ikhtiyar.
مبہم (mubham): Ambiguous; a word that can have multiple meanings without specification, such as 'ikhtartu' alone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the husband says 'ikhtari' and the wife responds 'ikhtartu' (without 'nafsi'), what is the ruling?
A) One raj'i divorce occurs.
B) One ba'in divorce occurs.
C) The divorce is invalid because 'nafs' was not mentioned.
D) Three divorces occur if the husband intended them.

Key Takeaway
For talaq via ikhtiyar, the word 'nafs' or its equivalent must be mentioned by either spouse; otherwise, the divorce is invalid.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Wife's Choice (Ikhtiyar) When Husband Says 'Ikhtari'
Explains ba'in divorce ruling by istihsan, rejecting qiyas, based on Sahaba ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wife's choice (ikhtiyar) when her husband says 'ikhtari', explain why the school prefers istihsan over qiyas, and identify the number of divorces that occur (one ba'in, not three).

Core Idea
When a husband says 'ikhtari', the wife's choice results in one ba'in divorce by istihsan, not zero by qiyas.

The Hanafi school recognizes a specific form of delegated divorce where the husband gives his wife the option to choose herself. This passage from Al-Hidayah explains that while strict analogy (qiyas) would suggest no divorce occurs, the school adopts an exceptional ruling based on juristic preference (istihsan) supported by the consensus of the Companions. The key implications are that only one ba'in divorce takes place, and the husband's intention for multiple divorces is irrelevant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Elements
The husband says 'ikhtari' (choose) to his wife, and she responds by choosing herself in the same sitting. Identify the parties: husband (the delegator) and wife (the delegate). Note that the wife must choose immediately in the same session.
If the wife does not choose in the same sitting, the delegation becomes void.
2
State the Qiyas Ruling
By strict qiyas, no divorce should occur. Reason: the husband does not own effecting divorce with this word himself, so he cannot delegate it to another. Understand that qiyas is the default method but is set aside here.
This qiyas argument would be persuasive if not for the stronger evidence.
3
Recognize the Istihsan Exception and Its Evidence
The Hanafi school rules by istihsan that one ba'in divorce does occur. The evidence is the ijma (consensus) of the Companions, particularly the practice of Ali (ra). This ijma overrides the qiyas.
Istihsan is a departure from qiyas for a stronger evidence; here it is the ijma.
4
Trace the Reasoning Behind Istihsan
The husband has the authority to keep or terminate the marriage, so he can make his wife his deputy in exercising that choice. When she chooses herself, it establishes her exclusive connection to herself, which is the essence of ba'in divorce.
The marriage bond is severed completely, making the divorce ba'in (irrevocable).
5
Analyze Indivisibility: Only One Divorce
Even if the husband intended three divorces, only one occurs. Ikhtiyar (choice) is indivisible—the wife chooses herself once and for all. This contrasts with explicit pronouncements where baynunah (separateness) can be graded (severe/light).
The ruling protects the wife from unintended multiple divorces.

Source Text

کتاب الطلاق
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
ترجمہ ... پس اگر اس عورت ) نے اپنے آپ کو اختیار کیا اس کے قول لفظ اختیاری کی صورت میں تو ایک بائنہ ہوگی ۔ اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ اس سے کچھ واقع نہ ہو۔ اگر چہ شوہر نے طلاق کی نیت کی ہو۔ کیونکہ شوہر اس لفظ سے واقع کرنے کا مالک نہیں ہے۔ پس اپنے علاوہ کی طرف بھی سپرد کرنے کا مالک نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن ہم نے اس کو استحسانا جائز جانا ہے۔ صحابہ کے اجماع کی وجہ سے۔ اور اسلئے کہ شوہر کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ وہ اسکے نکاح کو برابر قائم رکھے۔ یا اسکو جدا کر دے۔ پس شوہر اس عورت کو اپنا قائم مقام بنانے کا مالک ہو گا اس حکم میں ۔ پھر اس سے بائنہ ہی واقع ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اس عورت کا اپنے آپ کو اختیار کر نانفس کے ساتھ عورت کے اختصاص کو ثابت کرنے کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اور یہ بات بائن میں ہوگی۔ اور تین نہیں ہوں گی۔ اگر چہ شوہر نے اس کی نیت کی ہو۔ کیونکہ اختیار منقسم نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ بخلاف اہانت کے۔ اسلئے کہ بینونت منقسم ہوتی ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ شوہر کے لفظ اختیاری کہنے کے بعد اگر عورت نے اسی مجلس میں اپنے نفس کو اختیار کر لیا تو یہ ایک طلاق سے بائنہ ہوگی۔ یہی قول حضرت علی کا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ اس لفظ سے کوئی طلاق واقع نہ ہو۔ اگر چہ شوہر نے طلاق کی نیت کی ہو۔ کیونکہ شوہر اس لفظ سے خود طلاق واقع کرنے کا مالک نہیں ہے۔ لہذا دوسرے کو مالک بنانے کا کیسے نالک ہوگا۔ مگر صحابہ کے اجماع کی وجہ سے اس کو استحسانا جائز قرار دے دیا ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر کو یہ اختیار حاصل ہے کہ وہ اپنی بیوی کے نکاح کو قائم رکھے یا اس کو جدا کر دے۔ پس وہ اس اختیار میں اپنی بیوی کو اپنا قائم مقام بھی بنا سکتا ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فر ماتے ہیں کہ اس لفظ اختیاری سے ایک بائنہ واقع ہوگی کیونکہ عورت کا اپنے نفس کو اختیار کرنا اس وقت ثابت ہوگا جبکہ نفس کے ساتھ عورت کا اختصاص ثابت ہو جائے یعنی شوہر کی ملک زائل ہو جائے اور عورت اپنے نفس کی مالک ہو جائے اور ظاہر ہے کہ یہ بات طلاق بائن میں حاصل ہوگی۔ اور اگر شوہر نے تین طلاقوں کی نیت کی تو تین واقع نہیں ہوں گی۔ کیونکہ اختیار منقسم نہیں ہوتا۔ البتہ بینونت غلیظہ اور خفیفہ کی طرف منقسم ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس وجہ سے انت بائن میں تین طلاقوں کی نیت درست ہے۔ مگر اختیار کی صورت میں تین کی نیت صحیح نہیں ہے۔
Book of Divorce. Ashraf al-Bidaya Urdu Commentary on al-Hidayah Volume Four. Translation: So if this woman chose herself by his word 'ikhtiyari', then one ba'in divorce occurs. By qiyas, nothing should occur, even if the husband intended divorce, because the husband does not have ownership to effect divorce with this word, so he would not have ownership to delegate to another. But we have deemed it permissible by istihsan, due to the ijma of the Companions, and because the husband has the authority to keep the marriage or separate her. So the husband is owner to make her his deputy in this matter. Then from this, only ba'in occurs, because the woman's choosing herself establishes her exclusive connection with herself, which occurs in ba'in divorce. And three do not occur even if the husband intended three, because ikhtiyar (choice) is not divisible, unlike ihant (insult), because baynunah (separateness) is divisible. Clarification of the issue: After the husband says the word 'ikhtiyari', if the woman chooses herself in the same sitting, this is one ba'in divorce. This is the saying of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him). The author of al-Hidayah says that qiyas requires that no divorce occur with this word, even if the husband intended divorce, because the husband himself does not own effecting divorce with this word, so how can he own making another owner? But due to the ijma of the Companions, it has been deemed permissible by istihsan. A second proof is that the husband has the authority to keep his wife's marriage or separate her, so he can make his wife his deputy in this authority. The author of al-Hidayah says that with this word 'ikhtiyari', one ba'in divorce occurs, because the woman's choosing herself is proved only when her exclusive connection with herself is proved, i.e., the husband's ownership ceases and the woman becomes owner of herself, and this is clearly achieved in ba'in divorce. And if the husband intended three divorces, three do not occur, because ikhtiyar is not divisible. However, baynunah is divisible into severe and light, so in ihant, intending three divorces is valid, but in the case of ikhtiyar, intending three is not valid.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the effect of a husband telling his wife 'ikhtari' (choose). The author explains that by analogy (qiyas), this expression should not result in any divorce because the husband does not directly pronounce divorce nor does he have the authority to delegate divorce to another (since he cannot divorce by this word himself). However, the Hanafi school adopts an exception based on juristic preference (istihsan) supported by the consensus (ijma) of the Companions, particularly the practice of Ali (ra). The rationale is that the husband has the inherent authority to either keep the marriage or terminate it, so he may deputize his wife in exercising that choice. When she chooses herself, it establishes her exclusive right over herself, which is the essence of a ba'in divorce. Importantly, only one ba'in divorce occurs, not three, even if the husband intended three, because the concept of 'choice' is indivisible—the wife chooses herself once and for all, unlike situations where the husband explicitly pronounces three divorces. The commentary clarifies that this ruling is specific to the case where the husband uses the word 'ikhtari' and the wife responds in the same session.

Key Terms
اختیار (ikhtiyar): In this context, it refers to the husband giving his wife the option to choose herself, which when exercised results in divorce.
بائنہ (ba'inah): A divorce that immediately and completely severs the marriage bond, allowing remarriage only with a new contract (nikah).
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, a method of reasoning that deviates from strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling, based on a stronger evidence (like ijma or necessity).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the outcome when a husband tells his wife 'ikhtari' and she chooses herself in the same session?
A) No divorce occurs because the husband did not directly pronounce talaq.
B) One raj'i divorce occurs.
C) One ba'in divorce occurs, and three divorces do not occur even if intended.
D) Three ba'in divorces occur if the husband intended three.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a husband delegates divorce by saying 'ikhtari', the wife's choice results in one ba'in divorce, regardless of the husband's intention for multiple, because ikhtiyar is indivisible.

Condition of Mentioning 'Nafs' in Delegated Divorce
States requirement that word 'nafs' must appear in husband's or wife's speech for validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the requirement of mentioning 'nafs' in delegated divorce and explain the Hanafi proof from ijma and the mubham principle.

Core Idea
For a valid delegated divorce, the word 'nafs' must be uttered by either spouse; without it, no divorce occurs.

Delegated divorce (tafwid) allows a husband to empower his wife to divorce herself by saying 'ikhtari' (choose). However, the Hanafi school imposes a strict condition: the word 'nafs' (self) or its substitute must appear in the speech of either spouse. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proofs — the ijma of the Companions and the usul principle that an ambiguous expression cannot interpret another ambiguous expression.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is divorce by delegation (tafwid) when the husband says 'ikhtari' and the wife responds 'ikhtartu'. The ruling in Hanafi fiqh is that this is void unless one of them mentions 'nafs'.
The ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; other schools may differ.
2
Cite the first proof: Ijma
The passage states that the validity of delegated divorce with 'nafs' is known by ijma of the Companions. This ijma is an exception to qiyas, so it must be applied exactly as transmitted — including the requirement of 'nafs'.
Ijma here is qat'i in transmission and meaning.
3
Apply the second proof: Mubham principle
The husband's 'ikhtari' and the wife's 'ikhtartu' are both mubham (ambiguous). In Hanafi usul, one mubham cannot serve as interpretation (tafsir) for another mubham. Therefore, the wife's response does not specify divorce, and the act is void.
This principle reinforces the ijma-based ruling.
4
Address a potential objection
One might argue that the husband's intention (niyyah) specifies the divorce. The Hanafi response is that intention cannot resolve ambiguity on both sides; the spoken words must be clear.
Intention alone is insufficient when both utterances are mubham.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that if neither spouse mentions 'nafs' or its substitutes (ikhtiyaratu, tatliqatu), no divorce occurs. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
This is based on Zahir al-Riwayah and upheld by Al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولابد من ذكر النفس فى كلامه اوفى كلامها حتى لو قال لها اختارى فقالت قد اخترت فهو باطل لانه عرف بالاجماع وهو فى المفسر من احد الجانبين ولان المبهم لا يصلح تفسير اللمبهم ولاتعين مع الابهام
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور نفس کا ذکر ضروری ہے شوہر کے کلام میں یا عورت کے کلام میں حتی کہ اگر عورت سے کہا اختیاری۔ پھر عورت نے کہا اخترت تو یہ باطل ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ اجماع سے معلوم ہوا ہے اور اجماع آسمیں ہے کہ احد الجانبین میں تفسیر کی گئی ہو اور اسلئے کہ میہم مہم کی تغیر بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا ہے۔ اور ابہام کے ساتھ تعین نہیں ہوتی ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ لفظ اختیار سے طلاق واقع کرنے کیلئے زوجین میں سے کسی ایک کے کلام میں لفظ نفس یا اسکے قائم مقام کا مذکور ہونا ضروری ہے ( نفس کا قائم مقام لفظ اختیارۃ اور تطلیقہ ہے ) چنانچہ اگر شوہر نے اختاری کہا اور عورت نے جواب میں اخترت کہہ دیا تو طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ اختیار سے طلاق کا واقع ہونا صحابہ کے اجماع سے ثابت ہے۔ اور صحابہ کا اجماع اس صورت میں ہے جبکہ زوجین میں سے کسی ایک کے کلام میں لفظ نفس یا اس کا قائم مقام مذکور ہو۔ لہذا اجماع جس طرح وارد ہوا اس طرح رکھا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ اجماع خلاف قیاس ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہاں شوہر کا قول اختیاری مہم ہے۔ اور عورت کا قول جو اس کی تفسیر ہے وہ بھی مہم ہے۔ اور ایک مہم دوسرے مہم کی تفسیر واقع نہیں ہوتا۔ اس وجہ سے بھی یہ کلام باطل ہوگا۔ اور اگر آپ اشکال کریں کہ شوہر نے طلاق کی نیت کر کے طلاق کو متعین کر دیا ہے تو جواب یہ ہوگا کہ جانبین میں ابہام رہتے ہوئے طلاق کو متعین نہیں کیا جاسکتا ہے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: It is necessary to mention 'nafs' in his speech or her speech, so much so that if he says 'ikhtari' and she says 'qad ikhtartu', it is void, because it is known by ijma, and it (the ijma) is concerning the case where there is interpretation (tafsir) from one side, and because the ambiguous (mubham) cannot serve as interpretation for the ambiguous, and determination does not occur with ambiguity. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And the mention of 'nafs' is necessary in the husband's speech or the wife's speech, such that if he said 'ikhtari' and she said 'ikhtartu', it is void. Because this is known by ijma, and the ijma is that there is interpretation from one side, and because the ambiguous is not fit to be the interpretation of the ambiguous, and determination does not occur with ambiguity. Clarification: For divorce to occur with the word 'ikhtiyar', it is necessary that the word 'nafs' or its substitute be mentioned in the speech of either spouse (the substitutes for 'nafs' are the words 'ikhtiyaratu' and 'tatliqatu'). So if the husband said 'ikhtari' and the wife said 'ikhtartu' in response, no divorce occurs. The proof is that the occurrence of divorce with the word 'ikhtiyar' is established by the ijma of the Companions, and the ijma of the Companions is only in the case where the word 'nafs' or its substitute is mentioned in the speech of either spouse. Therefore, the ijma is applied as it came, because this ijma is contrary to qiyas. The second proof is that here the husband's statement 'ikhtari' is ambiguous (mubham), and the wife's statement which is its interpretation is also ambiguous, and one ambiguous cannot be interpretation for another ambiguous. For this reason also this speech is void. And if you object that the husband by intending divorce has specified it, then the answer is that with ambiguity on both sides, divorce cannot be specified.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage establishes a key condition for the validity of divorce by delegation (tafwid). The text, quoting al-Quduri, explains that the word 'nafs' (self) or its equivalent must appear in the speech of either the husband or the wife when the husband says 'ikhtari'. If the husband simply says 'ikhtari' and the wife responds 'ikhtartu' without mentioning 'nafs', the divorce is void. The reason is that the established ijma of the Companions regarding this practice only covers cases where 'nafs' is mentioned. Additionally, both utterances are considered ambiguous (mubham), and an ambiguous expression cannot serve as an interpretation for another ambiguous expression. The commentary also notes that the wife's intention does not help because the ambiguity remains. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school and is based on the strict application of the ijma, which is itself an exception to qiyas. The condition is strictly enforced: without 'nafs', no divorce occurs.

Key Terms
نفس (nafs): The word 'self' (nafs) as in 'ikhtari nafsak' (choose yourself). It is a required element for the validity of delegated divorce.
مبهم (mubham): Ambiguous or vague speech that does not specify a particular meaning without further context.
اجماع (ijma): Consensus of the scholars, specifically the Companions in this case, which establishes legal authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says 'ikhtari' (choose) and the wife responds 'ikhtartu' (I chose) without mentioning 'nafs', what is the ruling in the Hanafi school?
A) One ba'in divorce occurs.
B) No divorce occurs because 'nafs' was not mentioned.
C) One raj'i divorce occurs.
D) Three divorces occur because she chose.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires the word 'nafs' in delegated divorce, based on the strict scope of the Companions' ijma and the principle that mubham cannot interpret mubham.

Three Variants of Tafwid: When the Wife's Response Implicitly Accepts
Examines three subcases of delegated divorce phrasing and rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling (one ba'in divorce) for each of the three 'ikhtari' subcases and explain the linguistic principle of 'mufassar' and 'answer entails repetition'.

Core Idea
A wife's simple 'ikhtartu' in response to 'ikhtari nafsak' suffices for divorce because her reply implicitly repeats the clear subject.

This lesson examines three specific phrasing scenarios in delegated divorce (tafwid). You will learn how the Hanafi school resolves ambiguity through linguistic principles, ensuring that the wife's acceptance is valid even without repeating every word. The key is the classification of the husband's speech as clear (mufassar) or ambiguous, and the rule that a response contains the substance of the question.

Guided Path
1
Identify the husband's command
Note whether the command includes the word 'nafs' or 'ikhtiyara'. This determines whether his speech is clear (mufassar) or ambiguous.
In the first two subcases, the command is clear; in the third, it is ambiguous.
2
Analyze the wife's response
Determine if she explicitly says 'nafs' or simply says 'ikhtartu'. If she omits 'nafs', we must decide if her response implicitly refers to herself.
The rule 'answer entails repetition' is key.
3
Apply the rule of tafsir (clarification)
If the husband's speech is clear, the wife's simple 'ikhtartu' is understood as accepting the choice of herself. If the husband's speech is ambiguous, the wife's explicit 'nafs' clarifies it, but the husband's intent is required.
Tafsir can come from either side.
4
Determine the outcome
In all three subcases, one ba'in divorce occurs. However, in the third subcase, it is conditional on the husband having intended divorce at the time of his command.
The number of divorces is limited to one based on the wording 'ikhtiyara' or the nature of tafwid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرد نے کہا اختاری نفسک عورت نے کہا اخترت تو ایک طلاق بائنہ واقع ہو جاۓ گی
ولوقال اختاری نفسک فقالت اخترت تقع واحدة بائنة لان كلامه مفشر و كلامها خرج جوابا له فيتضمن اعادته وكذا لو قال اختارى اختيارة فقالت اخترت لان الهاء فى الاختيارة تنبئى عن الاتحاد والانفراد و اختيارها نفسها هو الذى يتحدمرة ويتعدد اخرى فصار مفسرا من جانبه ولوقال اختاری فقالت اخترت نفسى يقع الطلاق اذانوى الزوج لان كلامها مفسر و مانواه الزوج من محتملات كلامه
ترجمہ: اور اگر (شوہر) نے کہا تو اپنے نفس کو اختیار کر۔ عورت نے کہا میں نے اختیار کیا تو ایک بائنہ واقع ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ مرد کا کلام تفسیر کے ساتھ واقع ہوا ہے اور عورت کا کلام اس کے جواب میں نکلا ہے تو ( یہ ) مرد کے کلام کے لوٹانے کو متضمن ہو گا۔ اور ایسے ہی اگر کہا اختیار کرتو اختیار کرنا کیونکہ اختیارہ میں تا متحد اور منفرد ہونے کی خبر دیتی ہے۔ اور عورت کا اپنے نفس کو اختیار کرنا کبھی متحد ہوتا ہے اور کبھی متعدد ہوتا ہے تو مرد کی جانب سے کلام مفسر ہو گیا۔ اور اگر مرد نے کہا اختیار کر تو عورت نے کہا میں نے اپنے نفس کو اختیار کر لیا تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ بشرطیکہ شوہر نے نیت کی ہو۔ اسلئے کہ عورت کا کلام مفسر واقع ہوا ہے۔ اور شوہر نے جس چیز کی نیت کی ہے وہ شوہر کے کلام کے مشتملات میں سے ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ، مرد نے اپنی منکوحہ سے کہا اختاری نفسک عورت نے جواب میں اخترت کہا لفظ نفس ذکر نہیں کیا۔ تو ایک طلاق بائنہ واقع ہو جائے گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ مرد کا کلام لفظ نفس مذکور ہونے کی وجہ سے مفسر ہے۔ اور عورت کا کلام شوہر کے کلام کے جواب میں واقع ہوا ہے۔ لہذا عورت کا کلام شوہر کے کلام کے اعادہ کو متضمن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ قاعدہ ہے کہ جواب مافی السوال کے اعادہ کو متضمن ہوتا ہے۔ مثلاً کسی نے سوال کیا کہ کیا زید نے مارا۔ آپ نے جواب میں فرمایا جی ہاں۔ تو یہ لفظ جی ہاں۔ زید نے مارا کو متضمن ہے۔ تو اب عورت کے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہوگا کہ جس چیز کا تو نے مجھ کو حکم دیا ہے اپنے اختیار ہے۔ اس کو میں نے اختیار کیا۔ اور مرد نے اختیار دیا تھا نفس کے بارے میں۔ پس عورت کی جانب سے بھی نفس ہی کو اختیار کرنا ہوگا نہ کہ کسی اور چیز کو۔
دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مرد نے کہا اختاری اختیارةُ - عورت نے جواب میں اخترت کہا تو طلاق بائنہ واقع ہو جائے گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اختیارہ میں تا وحدت کیلئے ہے۔ اب شوہر کے کلام کا منشاء یہ ہوگا کہ شوہر اپنی عورت کو ایسی چیز کا اختیار دینا چاہتا ہے۔ جس میں وحدت اور تعدد ہوتا ہے اور وحدت اور تعدد صرف اس میں ہے کہ عورت اپنے نفس کو اختیار کرے۔ اس لئے کہ اگر عورت نے ایک طلاق کے ساتھ اپنے نفس کو اختیار کر لے۔ اس لئے کہ اگر عورت نے ایک طلاق کے ساتھ اپنے نفس کو اختیار کیا ہے۔ تو اس اختیار میں وحدت پائی گئی۔
The man said 'ikhtari nafsak', the woman said 'ikhtartu', so one ba'in divorce occurs. And if he said 'ikhtari nafsak' and she said 'ikhtartu', one ba'in divorce occurs because his speech is clarified (mufassar) and her speech came as a response to him, so it entails repeating it. Similarly, if he said 'ikhtari ikhtiyara' and she said 'ikhtartu', because the 'ha' in 'ikhtiyara' indicates unity and singularity, and her choosing herself is that which is sometimes single and sometimes multiple, so his speech became clarified from his side. And if he said 'ikhtari' and she said 'ikhtartu nafsi', the divorce occurs if the husband intended, because her speech is clarified and what the husband intended is among the probabilities of his speech. Translation: And if (the husband) said 'choose yourself', and the woman said 'I chose', then one ba'in divorce occurs. Because the man's speech is clarified, and the woman's speech came in response to him, so it entails repeating his speech. Similarly, if he said 'choose an ikhtiyara', because the 'ha' in 'ikhtiyara' indicates unity and singularity, and her choosing herself is that which is sometimes single and sometimes multiple, so his speech became clarified from his side. And if the man said 'choose' and the woman said 'I chose myself', the divorce occurs provided the husband intended, because her speech is clarified and what the husband intended is among the possibilities of his speech. Clarification: The man said to his wife 'ikhtari nafsak', the wife responded 'ikhtartu' without mentioning the word 'nafs'. So one ba'in divorce occurs. The proof is that the man's speech is clarified because the word 'nafs' is mentioned, and the woman's speech came in response to the husband's speech. Therefore, her speech entails repeating his speech. Because the principle is that the answer entails repeating what is in the question. For example, someone asked: 'Did Zaid beat?' You replied 'Yes.' So the word 'yes' entails 'Zaid beat.' So the meaning of the woman's response is: 'That which you commanded me, to choose, I have chosen it.' And the man gave the option regarding the self, so from the woman's side, she must have chosen the self and not something else. The second issue is that the man said 'ikhtari ikhtiyara', the woman responded 'ikhtartu', so one ba'in divorce occurs. The proof is that 'ikhtiyara' has a 'ta' for unity. Now the import of the husband's speech is that he wants to give his woman an option that involves both unity and multiplicity, and unity and multiplicity is only in her choosing herself. Because if the woman chooses herself with one divorce, then in that choice unity is found.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage presents three subcases of the delegation of divorce (tafwid). In the first case, the husband says 'ikhtari nafsak' (choose yourself) and the wife simply responds 'ikhtartu' (I chose) without repeating 'nafs'. Even without the wife explicitly saying 'nafs', the divorce occurs because the husband's speech was clear (mufassar) by containing 'nafs'. The wife's response, being an answer to his command, implicitly repeats the subject (nafs) as per the linguistic principle that a response contains the substance of the question. In the second case, the husband says 'ikhtari ikhtiyara' using the word 'ikhtiyara' (which ends with the feminine 'ta' indicating unity). The word 'ikhtiyara' implies a single act of choice, and this meaning is made clear from the husband's side. Even though the wife only says 'ikhtartu', the divorce occurs because the husband's wording specifies the option is for her to choose herself (which can be single or multiple). The 'ta' in 'ikhtiyara' indicates that the option is for a single divorce, but the underlying reference is to the self. In the third case, the husband says just 'ikhtari' (ambiguous) and the wife says 'ikhtartu nafsi' (I chose myself). Here, the wife's speech clarifies the ambiguity. The divorce occurs only if the husband intended divorce, because his ambiguous statement could encompass divorce if he so intended. Her response specifies the meaning. In all three cases, the result is one ba'in divorce due to the presence of tafsir (clarification) from one side.

Key Terms
مفسر (mufassar): Clear or unambiguous speech that does not require further explanation. In this context, the husband's speech is mufassar when it includes 'nafs' or 'ikhtiyara'.
اختیارة (ikhtiyarah): A noun form meaning 'a single choice' (feminine with ta). Used to indicate that the option is for one divorce.
قائم مقام (qa'im maqam): Substitute or deputy; here, the wife acts as the husband's deputy in exercising the choice to divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a husband says 'ikhtari nafsak' and the wife responds 'ikhtartu' (without saying 'nafs'), what is the ruling?
A) No divorce occurs because she did not explicitly choose herself.
B) One ba'in divorce occurs because her response implicitly repeats the husband's clear command.
C) Three divorces occur because she chose without limit.
D) One raj'i divorce occurs because the word 'ikhtartu' is ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi delegated divorce, the wife's acceptance is interpreted in light of the husband's clear command; ambiguity is resolved by tafsir and the principle that the answer entails repetition.

Wife's 'Ikhtartu' Response to 'Ikhtari Nafsak': Hanafi Divorce Ruling
Ruling on divorce when wife says 'ikhtartu' to husband's delegation of choice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a wife responds 'ikhtartu' to her husband's delegation of choice, and distinguish the conditions under which divorce occurs.

Core Idea
When a husband says 'Choose yourself' and the wife says 'I chose', one irrevocable divorce occurs because her reply is deemed to include herself.

In this passage, we examine a specific scenario of delegated divorce (tafwid). The husband uses the phrase 'ikhtari nafsak' (choose yourself), and the wife responds only 'ikhtartu' (I chose) without explicit reference to herself. The Hanafi school rules that this is sufficient for one bain divorce. The reasoning involves the principle that a response repeats the content of the command, making her choice apply to her person. We also explore variations where the husband's speech is more or less explicit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the husband's phrase
Determine whether the husband said 'ikhtari nafsak' (explicit choice of self), 'ikhtari ikhtiyarah' (choice of a choice), or simply 'ikhtari' (choose, ambiguous).
The first two are considered mufassar (interpretative); the third is ambiguous.
2
Identify the wife's response
Note whether she said 'ikhtartu' (I chose) or 'ikhtartu nafsi' (I chose myself). The ruling may differ depending on the husband's original phrase.
In the first two scenarios, 'ikhtartu' suffices; in the third, she must say 'ikhtartu nafsi' for divorce to occur (if husband intended).
3
Apply the response repetition principle
Understand that a response to a command is deemed to repeat the command's content. Therefore, 'ikhtartu' in reply to 'ikhtari nafsak' is interpreted as 'ikhtartu nafsi'.
This principle is supported by analogy with everyday questions: e.g., 'Did Zayd hit?' answered 'Yes' implies 'Yes, Zayd hit.'
4
Determine the type of divorce
Conclude that one bain (irrevocable) divorce occurs in the first two scenarios, and in the third scenario it occurs only if the husband intended divorce.
The number is always one because the wife's choice is singular; she cannot effect three divorces unless explicitly given that authority.
5
Consider the third scenario
When the husband says only 'ikhtari', his speech is ambiguous. The wife's explicit 'ikhtartu nafsi' is mufassar, but divorce depends on his intention because the ambiguity leaves room for other possibilities (e.g., choosing a gift).
If he intends divorce, it occurs; otherwise not.

A man said, 'Choose yourself.' The woman said, 'I chose.' Then one irrevocable divorce occurs. And if he said, 'Choose yourself,' and she said, 'I chose,' it occurs as one irrevocable divorce because his speech is interpretative and her speech comes as a response to him, so it includes repetition of his speech. Similarly, if he said, 'Choose; [it is] a choice,' and she said, 'I chose,' because the 'ha' in 'al-ikhtiyarah' indicates oneness and uniqueness, and her choice of herself is that which is sometimes singular and sometimes multiple, so it becomes interpretative from his side. And if he said, 'Choose,' and she said, 'I chose myself,' divorce occurs if the husband intended, because her speech is interpretative and what the husband intended is among the possibilities of his speech.

Commentary
This passage presents the first scenario of talaq bi al-ikhtiyar. The husband uses the explicit phrase 'ikhtari nafsak' (choose yourself), and the wife responds only 'ikhtartu' (I chose) without mentioning 'nafsi'. The ruling is that one bain (irrevocable) divorce occurs. The reasoning is twofold: (1) The husband's speech is interpretative (mufassar) because it includes the word 'nafsak', making the object clear; (2) The wife's reply is a response to his command, and by the principle that a response repeats the content of the question, her 'ikhtartu' effectively means 'I chose myself.' This is analogized to a question like 'Did Zayd hit?' and the answer 'Yes' implying 'Yes, Zayd hit.' Thus, the wife's choice automatically applies to her own person, resulting in divorce.

Key Terms
بائنہ (bā'inah): A divorce that is irrevocable; the husband cannot take the wife back without a new marriage and intervening marriage to another.
مفسر (mufassar): A clear or interpretative statement that leaves no ambiguity about its meaning.
اختیار (ikhtiyār): The act of choosing; here it refers to the husband giving his wife the choice to divorce herself or not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) One irrevocable divorce (bain) occurs.
D) Three divorces occur.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a husband explicitly delegates choice to his wife (e.g., 'choose yourself'), her simple reply 'I chose' suffices for one irrevocable divorce, as her response is legally deemed to repeat his command including herself.

Divorce by 'Ikhtari Ikhtiyaratan': One Bain Divorce
Ruling on divorce when husband says 'ikhtari ikhtiyaratan'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband says 'ikhtari ikhtiyaratan' and explain why the 'ta' of unity constrains the divorce to one bain divorce.

Core Idea
The 'ta' in 'ikhtiyaratan' indicates singular choice, so the wife's acceptance yields one irrevocable divorce.

In this lesson, we examine the second scenario of choice-based divorce: the husband uses the phrase 'ikhtari ikhtiyaratan'. The addition of 'ikhtiyaratan' with the feminine 'ta' of oneness changes the meaning compared to the simple 'ikhtari'. Understanding the grammatical nuance is key to deriving the correct legal outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wording
The husband says 'ikhtari ikhtiyaratan' – 'Choose, [it is] a choice.' Focus on the word 'ikhtiyaratan'.
2
Analyze the grammatical marker
The 'ta' at the end of 'ikhtiyaratan' is ta al-wahdah (the ta of unity). In Arabic, this indicates a singular instance.
3
Understand the nature of choice
The wife's act of choosing herself (ikhtiyar al-nafs) can theoretically be realized with one divorce or three divorces. The 'ta' restricts it to one.
4
Apply the Hanafi rule of tafsir
Because the wording is ambiguous but the 'ta' clarifies singularity, the husband's statement is considered mufassar (interpreted) as 'choose yourself with one choice'.
Mufassar means the ambiguity is resolved by a contextual or grammatical indicator.
5
Conclude the ruling
Upon the wife's reply 'ikhtartu' (I chose), one bain divorce takes effect.

The second issue is that a man said, 'Choose; [it is] a choice.' The woman replied, 'I chose.' Then an irrevocable divorce occurs. The evidence is that the 'ta' in 'ikhtiyarah' is for oneness. Now the husband's speech means that the husband wants to give his wife a choice in something that has oneness and multiplicity, and oneness and multiplicity are only in that the wife chooses herself. Because if the wife chooses herself with one divorce, then in this choice there is oneness; and if she chooses with three divorces, then in that choice there is multiplicity. So from the husband's side the speech becomes interpretative, as if the man said, 'Choose yourself.'

Commentary
This passage explains the second scenario: the husband uses the verbal noun 'ikhtiyaratan' with the 'ta' of unity at the end. The 'ta' here indicates that the choice is singular or unified. The ruling is again one bain divorce. The reasoning is that the husband's choice phrase, despite being ambiguous, becomes interpretative because the nature of choice of self can be either single (one divorce) or multiple (three divorces). Since the 'ta' implies oneness, it effectively means 'choose yourself with one choice.' Thus the husband's statement is treated as mufassar, and the wife's response 'ikhtartu' again picks up that meaning, resulting in one divorce.

Key Terms
اختیارة (ikhtiyāratun): A verbal noun meaning 'a choice', with the ta of unity (ta al-wahda) attached to indicate a single act of choosing.
وحدت (waḥdat): Oneness, singularity.

The presence of ta al-wahdah in 'ikhtiyaratan' makes the husband's delegation of choice singular, so the wife's acceptance results in one bain divorce.

Wife Says 'Ana Akhtar Nafsi' After 'Ikhtari': Divorce if Husband Intends
Ruling and istihsan for divorce when wife uses present tense 'akhtar' with 'nafsi'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a wife's response of 'ana akhtar nafsi' effects divorce and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.

Core Idea
A wife's present tense 'I choose myself' effects divorce because it describes a current choice, unlike a mere promise.

This lesson deals with a specific scenario in Hanafi divorce law: when a husband says simply 'ikhtari' (choose) and the wife replies 'ana akhtar nafsi' (I choose myself). Strict analogy (qiyas) would suggest no divorce because the present tense could indicate a future promise. However, the Hanafi school adopts istihsan (juristic preference) based on the Prophetic precedent of Aisha (ra) and the linguistic reality of the verb 'akhtar'. Understanding this reasoning sharpens your ability to apply usul principles in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the precise ruling: one bain divorce occurs if the husband intended divorce when he said 'ikhtari'. Note that the wife's phrase 'ana akhtar nafsi' is key.
The husband's intention is required because 'ikhtari' is ambiguous (mujmal).
2
Understand the qiyas counterargument
Qiyas compares this to the case of 'tallaqi nafsak' (divorce yourself) where the wife's present tense response does not effect divorce. The present tense can signify future, so 'akhtar' could be a promise, not an immediate act.
The qiyas relies on the ambiguity of the mudari' verb.
3
Analyze the istihsan evidence
The primary evidence is the hadith of Aisha (ra) when the Prophet (saw) offered choice; she said 'I choose Allah and His Messenger' using the present tense, and the Prophet accepted it as a valid choice. Also, 'akhtar' is haqiqah for the present state (a current decision), unlike 'ullaqu' which cannot describe a continuous state.
This linguistic distinction is crucial in Hanafi usul.
4
Apply the ruling to the scenario
Since istihsan overrides qiyas, the wife's response is taken as an immediate choice, effecting divorce if the husband intended divorce. The result is one bain divorce.
The husband's intention transforms a potential ambiguity into a definite divorce.

Source Text

تیسرا مسئلہ، اگر مرد نے کہا اختیاری۔ عورت نے جواب میں کہا اخترت نفسی اور شوہر نے طلاق کی نیت کی ہے۔ تو اس صورت میں بھی ایک طلاق بائن واقع ہو جائے گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت کا کلام تو مفسر ہے اور شوہر نے جس چیز کی نیت کی ہے۔ یعنی طلاق کی وہ اس کے کلام کے محتملات میں سے ہے۔ شوہر نے اختاری کہا عورت نے انا اختار نفسی کہا تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ ولوقال اختارى فقالت انا اختار نفسى فهى طالق والقياس ان لا تطلق لان هذا مجرد وعد او يحتمله فصار كما اذاقال لها طلقى نفسك فقالت انا اطلق نفسى وجه الاستحسان حديث عائشة رضى الله عنها فانها قالت لابل اختار الله و رسوله واعتبره النبي عليه السلام جوابا منها ولان هذه الصيغة حقيقة في الحال وتجوز فى الاستقبال كما فى كلمة الشهادة واداء الشهادة بخلاف قولها اطلق نفسى لانه تعذر جمله على الحال لانه ليس بحكاية عن حالة قائمة و الاكذلك قولها انا اختار نفسى لانه حكاية عن حالة قائمة وهو اختيارها نفسها ترجمہ اور اگر مرد نے کہا اختیار کر تو عورت نے کہا میں اختیار کرتی ہوں اپنے نفس کو تو یہ مطلقہ ہے۔ اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ طلاق واقع نہ ہو ۔ کیونکہ یہ محض وعدہ ہے۔ یا اس کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ عورت سے کہا تو اپنے آپ کو طلاق دے دے۔ اس نے کہا کہ میں اپنے نفس کو طلاق دیتی ہوں ۔ وجہ استحسان حدیث عائشہ ہے۔ اسلئے کہ حضرت عائشہ نے کہا نہیں بلکہ میں اللہ اور اداء شہادت میں بخلاف اس کے قول اطلق نفسی کے، کیونکہ اس کو حال پر محمول کرنا متعذر ہے کیونکہ وہ حالت موجودہ کی حکایت نہیں ہے۔ اور اس کا قول اختیار نفسی ایسا نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ حالت قائمہ کی حکایت ہے اور وہ اس کا اپنے نفس کو اختیار کرنا ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ مرد نے اپنی منکوحہ سے کہا اختاری بیوی نے کہا انا اختار نفسی تو اس سے طلاق بائن ہو جائے گی اور قیاس کا مقتضی یہ ہے کہ طلاق واقع نہ ہو وجہ قیاس یہ ہے کہ عورت نے اختبار فعل مضارع استعمال کیا ہے۔ اور فعل مضارع حال اور استقبال دونوں کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ پس اگر عورت نے استقبال مراد لیا تو یہ محض وعدہ ہو گا۔ اور محض وعدہ طلاق سے طلاق واقع نہیں ہوتی ۔ اور اگر حال مراد لیا ہے تو کم از کم استقبال کا احتمال ہے۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ شوہر نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا طلقی نفسک اس کی بیوی نے جواب میں انا اطلق نفسی کہا اور اس سے طلاق واقع نہیں ہوتی ۔ لہذا انا اختار نفسی سے بھی طلاق واقع نہ ہونی چاہئے ۔ وجه استحسان .. حديث عائشہ ہے۔ روایت کیا گیا ہے کہ جب آیت پایها النبی قل لازواجک ان کنتن تردن الحيوة الدنيا و زينتها فتعالین امتعكن و اسر حکن سراحا جمیلا نازل ہوئی تو حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت عائشہ سے فرمایا کہ میں تجھ کو ایک بات
The third issue: if a man said, 'Choose,' and the woman replied, 'I chose myself' and the husband intended divorce, then in this case also one irrevocable divorce occurs. The evidence is that the woman's speech is interpretative and what the husband intended (i.e., divorce) is among the possibilities of his speech. If the husband said 'Choose,' and the woman said 'I choose myself,' then she is divorced. And analogical reasoning (qiyas) would dictate that she is not divorced, because this is merely a promise or it can bear that [meaning]. So it becomes like when he said to her, 'Divorce yourself,' and she said, 'I divorce myself.' The basis of istihsan is the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that she said, 'Rather, I choose Allah and His Messenger,' and the Prophet (peace be upon him) considered it as a valid response from her. And because this phrase (ikhtaru) is haqiqah for the present tense and figurative for the future, as in the word of testimony (kalimat al-shahada) and the performance of testimony. Contrary to her saying 'I divorce myself' because it is impossible to apply it to the present state since it is not a narration of an existing situation. And her saying 'I choose myself' is not like that because it is a narration of an existing situation, and that is her choosing herself. Explanation: the husband said to his wife 'Choose.' The wife said 'I choose myself.' Then one bain divorce occurs. The requirement of qiyas is that divorce does not occur. The reason for qiyas is that the woman used the present tense verb (fi'l mudari'), and the present tense can bear both present and future meanings. So if the woman meant the future, it is a mere promise, and a mere promise does not effect divorce. And if she meant the present, at least there is the possibility of the future. So this becomes like when the husband says to his wife 'Divorce yourself' and she replies 'I divorce myself,' from which divorce does not occur. Therefore, from 'I choose myself' also divorce should not occur. The basis of istihsan is the hadith of Aisha. It is narrated that when the verse was revealed, 'O Prophet, say to your wives, if you desire the life of this world and its adornment, then come, I will give you provision and release you with a good release,' the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Aisha, 'I will tell you a matter...'
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage discusses the third scenario where the husband simply says 'Ikhtari' (choose) without any additional word like 'nafsak' or 'ikhtiyaratan', and the wife responds with the full present tense phrase 'Ana akhtar nafsi' (I choose myself). The ruling is that one bain divorce occurs, but only if the husband intended divorce. The text presents a qiyas (analogical reasoning) that would suggest no divorce: because the present tense verb can indicate future, making it a mere promise, similar to the case of 'Tallaqi nafsak' (divorce yourself) where the wife's response 'Ana ullaqu nafsi' does not effect divorce. However, the Hanafi school adopts istihsan (juristic preference) based on two proofs: (1) The hadith of Aisha (ra) where the Prophet (saw) gave her the choice (takhayyur) to stay or leave, and she said 'Rather, I choose Allah and His Messenger,' which the Prophet accepted as a valid choice; (2) The phrase 'Akhtar' is haqiqah (literal) for the present state and only figurative for the future, unlike 'Ullaqu' which cannot be applied to the present because divorce is not a continuous state. Thus, the wife's statement is taken as a present choice, making it effective immediately. The husband's intention is required because his word 'Ikhtari' is ambiguous (mujmal) and his niyyah specifies divorce.

Key Terms
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning; here the qiyas would compare 'ikhtari' to 'tallaqi nafsak' and conclude no divorce due to the ambiguity of the present tense.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method that departs from strict qiyas due to stronger evidence (here, the hadith of Aisha) or to achieve a more appropriate ruling.
فعل مضارع (fiʿl muḍāriʿ): The present tense verb in Arabic, which can denote both present and future time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school use istihsan to rule that 'ana akhtar nafsi' effects divorce, despite the qiyas suggesting otherwise?
A) Because the husband explicitly intended divorce.
B) Because of the hadith of Aisha (ra) and the nature of the present tense verb.
C) Because the wife's statement is a promise.
D) Because divorce is always preferred as a ruling.

Key Takeaway
When a wife says 'ana akhtar nafsi' in response to 'ikhtari', istihsan based on the hadith of Aisha and linguistic reality makes it an immediate choice, effecting one bain divorce if the husband intended divorce.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
15 min
The Ruling on 'Ikhtari' and 'Ana Akhtar Nafsi': One Talaq Bain
Ruling with proof from hadith and qiyas/istihsan analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband says 'ikhtari' and the wife responds 'ana akhtar nafsi', and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas using the hadith of Aisha and linguistic principles.

Core Idea
When the wife says 'I choose myself' in the present tense, one talaq bain occurs—the present tense is literal, not a future promise.

The Hanafi school addresses a subtle point in delegation of divorce: if the husband gives his wife the option to choose (ikhtiyar) and she responds in the present tense, does divorce occur immediately? At first glance, qiyas suggests it is a mere promise. However, a sahih hadith and a linguistic principle shift the ruling to an immediate effect. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning, showing how istihsan overrides analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the husband's statement and wife's response
The husband says 'ikhtari' (choose), the wife says 'ana akhtar nafsi' (I choose myself). The context includes the husband's intent for divorce, but no additional explicit words.
The wife's response uses the present tense verb 'akhtar'.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
One talaq bain (irrevocable divorce) occurs. This is the mufta bihi position based on istihsan.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Analyze the qiyas (analogy) that would deny divorce
Qiyas analogizes this case to 'taliqi nafsak' (divorce yourself) where the wife says 'ana utliqu nafsi' (I divorce myself). In that case, no divorce occurs because the present tense could be a future promise. Similarly, 'ana akhtar nafsi' could be a promise, so qiyas says no divorce.
The analogy rests on the ambiguity of the present tense.
4
Examine the istihsan (juristic preference)
Istihsan is based on the hadith of Aisha (RA) when the Prophet (SAW) gave her the choice after revelation of Surah al-Ahzab verse 28. She responded with the present tense 'akhtar' (I choose), and the Prophet accepted it as an immediate choice. This shows the present tense can be effective for choice.
The hadith is Sahih (Bukhari, Muslim).
5
Understand the linguistic distinction
The word 'utliqu' (I divorce) is an act of the tongue; it cannot narrate an existing state because before uttering it, no divorce exists. 'Akhtar' (I choose) is an act of the heart; the tongue narrates an existing choice. Thus, 'ana akhtar nafsi' is a narration of a present act, not a future promise.
Linguistically, the present tense is literal for present and metaphorical for future; here it is taken literally.

دوسری وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ صیغہ مضارع حال کے معنی میں حقیقت ہے اور استقبال میں مجاز ہے۔ اور حقیقت کا مراد لینا بھی ممکن ہے۔ لہذا یہاں حال کے معنی مراد ہوں گے جیسا کہ کلمہ شہادت اشهد ان لا اله الا الله و اشهد ان محمداً عبده ورسوله مین ایمان کا اعتبار کیا ہے نہ کہ وعدہ ایمان کا۔ درانحالیکہ اس میں صیغہ مضارع سے شہادت دی گئی ہے۔ اور ایسے ہی جب کسی گواہ نے کہا اشهد بكذا ۔ اس میں حال مراد ہے۔ پس جب یہ ثابت ہو گیا کہ حال حقیقت ہے تو مجاز یعنی استقبال کی طرف رجوع نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ انا اختار نفسی کو انا اطلق نفسی پر قیاس کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ اطلق کو حال کے معنی پر محمول کرنا متعذر ہے۔ اور اختیار کو حال کے معنی پر محمول کرنا متعذر نہیں۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ طلاق دینا زبان کا عمل ہے نہ کہ دل کا۔ اور کسی چیز کو اختیار کرنا قلب کا عمل ہے۔ دوسری بات یہ ذہن نشین کر لیجئے کہ حکایت وجود محکی عنہ کا تقاضا کرتی ہے۔ پس جس کی حکایت کی گئی ہے وہ حکایت کرنے سے پہلے موجود ہونا چاہئے ۔ پس لفظ اطلق کو حال پر محمول کرنا ناممکن اسلئے ہے کہ اگر حال کے معنی پر محمول کیا گیا تو یہ حکایت ہو گا۔ حالانکہ یہ کی حالت موجودہ کی حکایت نہیں ہوسکتا۔ کیونکہ اس لفظ کا تلفظ کرنے سے پہلے کوئی ایسی چیز موجود نہیں جس کو محکی عنہ بنایا جاتا۔ برخلاف انا اختار کے۔ کیونکہ یہ لفظ حالت موجودہ کی حکایت ہو سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اختیار قلب کا عمل ہے۔ پس زبان سے ذکر کرنا دل میں موجود امر کی حکایت ہوگا۔
Book of Divorce. Ashraf al-Bidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume Four. And if he gave her the option with three divorces, then in that option there will be multiplicity. So the husband's speech becomes explicated, as if the man said: 'You may choose yourself.' Third issue: If the man said: 'Ikhtari' (choose). The woman replied: 'Akhtartu nafsi' (I choose myself) and the husband intended divorce. In this case also, one irrevocable divorce (talaq bain) occurs. The proof is that the woman's speech is explicated (mufassar) and what the husband intended, i.e., divorce, is among the possibilities of her speech. The husband said 'Ikhtari', the woman said 'Ana akhtar nafsi', so divorce occurs. And if he says 'Ikhtari' and she says 'Ana akhtar nafsi', she is divorced. Qiyas dictates that she should not be divorced because this is merely a promise or has that possibility. So it becomes like when he said to her 'Taliqi nafsak' (divorce yourself) and she said 'Ana utliqu nafsi' (I divorce myself). The basis of istihsan is the hadith of Aisha (RA) that she said: 'Rather, I choose Allah and His Messenger.' The Prophet (SAW) considered it a valid response from her. And because this form (ikhtaru) is literal (haqiqah) in the present and metaphorical (majaz) in the future, as in the word of testimony (shahadah) and bearing witness. Unlike her saying 'Utliqu nafsi' because it is impossible to carry it upon the present tense, as it is not a narration of an existing state. And it is not like her saying 'Ana akhtar nafsi' because it is a narration of an existing state, which is her choosing herself. Translation: And if the man said 'Ikhtari' (choose) and the woman said 'I choose myself', then she is divorced. Qiyas is that divorce should not occur, because this is merely a promise or has that possibility. Thus it becomes like when he said to her 'Taliqi nafsak' and she said 'I divorce myself'. Basis of istihsan: the hadith of Aisha. Because Aisha said: 'Rather, I choose Allah and His Messenger' and the Prophet (SAW) considered it a valid response from her. And because this word 'ikhtaru' is literal in the present and metaphorical in the future. As in the word of testimony (shahadah) and bearing witness. Unlike her saying 'Utliqu nafsi' because it is impossible to carry it upon the present tense, because it is not a narration of an existing state. And her saying 'Akhtar nafsi' is not like that because it is a narration of an existing state, which is her choosing herself. Elaboration of the case: The man said to his wife 'Ikhtari', the wife said 'Ana akhtar nafsi', so an irrevocable divorce (talaq bain) occurs. Qiyas requires that divorce should not occur. The basis of qiyas is that the woman used a present tense verb (fi'l mudari'), and the present tense has the possibility of both present and future. So if the woman intended the future, it is a mere promise, and a mere promise does not effect divorce. And if she intended the present, then at least there is the possibility of the future. Thus it becomes like when the husband said to his wife 'Taliqi nafsak' and his wife replied 'Ana utliqu nafsi', and divorce does not occur from that. Therefore, 'Ana akhtar nafsi' should also not effect divorce. Basis of istihsan: the hadith of Aisha. It is narrated that when the verse 'O Prophet, say to your wives: If you desire the life of this world and its adornment, then come, I will provide for you and give you a gracious release' was revealed, the Prophet (SAW) said to Aisha: 'I will inform you of a matter, but do not answer without consulting your parents.' Then he informed her of the verse. Aisha said: 'Should I consult my parents regarding this? No, rather I choose Allah and His Messenger and the Hereafter.' The Prophet (SAW) considered Aisha's response valid, even though Aisha used the present tense form, which has the possibility of the future. So from the hadith of Aisha, it is understood that the present tense form also establishes choice (ikhtiyar). Second basis of istihsan: The present tense form is literal in the meaning of the present and metaphorical in the future. It is possible to take it in the literal sense. Therefore, here the meaning of the present will be taken. As in the word of testimony 'Ashhadu an la ilaha illallah wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan abduhu wa rasuluhu', faith is considered, not a promise of faith, even though testimony is given with the present tense form. Similarly, when a witness says 'Ashhadu bi kadha', the present is intended. So when it is established that the present is literal, one does not revert to the metaphorical (future). The author of Hidayah says: It is not correct to analogize 'Ana akhtar nafsi' to 'Ana utliqu nafsi'. Because 'utliqu' cannot be carried upon the present, while 'akhtar' can. The reason is that divorce is an act of the tongue, not the heart, whereas choice (ikhtiyar) is an act of the heart. Another point: Narration (hikayah) requires the existence of the narrated matter. So what is narrated must exist before the narration. Thus, carrying the word 'utliqu' upon the present is impossible because if carried upon the present, it would be a narration, but it cannot be a narration of an existing state, because before uttering this word, there is nothing that can be made the object of narration. Contrary to 'Ana akhtar', because this word can be a narration of an existing state, since choice is an act of the heart. So mentioning it by the tongue is a narration of what exists in the heart.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Book of Divorce (Kitab al-Talaq) concerning the phrase 'ikhtari' (choose) used by the husband. The passage addresses the third mas'ala (issue) in a sequence: if the husband gives the wife the option to choose herself, and she says 'I choose myself', one talaq bain occurs. The author first states the ruling, then addresses the qiyas (analogy) that would suggest no divorce occurs because the wife's statement could be a future promise. The basis of istihsan (juristic preference) is the famous hadith of Aisha (RA) when the Prophet (SAW) gave her the choice (takhyir) after the revelation of Surah al-Ahzab verse 28. Aisha responded with the present tense 'akhtar' (I choose), and the Prophet considered it a valid acceptance. This shows that the present tense can be effective for choice. Additionally, the author provides a linguistic argument: the present tense form (mudari') is literal for the present and metaphorical for the future; since the literal meaning is possible, it is preferable. The author of Hidayah distinguishes this from the case where the husband says 'taliqi nafsak' (divorce yourself) and the wife responds 'ana utliqu nafsi' (I divorce myself), which does not effect divorce because 'uttering divorce' is an act of the tongue, not a narration of an existing state, unlike 'choosing' which is an act of the heart. Thus, the wife's response is considered a present act of choice, resulting in one talaq bain.

Key Terms
اختیار (ikhtiyar): The option given to the wife to choose herself, resulting in talaq if she chooses herself.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference based on a stronger evidence (here, the hadith of Aisha) overriding qiyas.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning based on the similarity of the present case to 'taliqi nafsak'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No talaq (mere promise)
B) One talaq raj'i
C) One talaq bain
D) Three talaqs

Key Takeaway
When the husband gives the option (ikhtiyar) and the wife responds with present tense 'I choose myself', one talaq bain occurs immediately by istihsan, overriding the analogy to 'taliqi nafsak'.

Repetition of 'Ikhtari' and Wife's Response: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on talaq via repetition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the repetition of 'ikhtari' and distinguish between the rulings of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, citing their respective proofs.

Core Idea
Repetition of 'ikhtari' indicates multiple delegations; Abu Hanifa rules three divorces, Sahibayn only one.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the legal effect when a husband says 'ikhtari' three times to his wife, and she responds by choosing herself three times. The disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hinges on whether the repetition of the word creates multiple separate delegations or a single one. Understanding this case sharpens your ability to parse nuanced legal arguments based on language and intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the dispute
Read the passage and note the husband's triple use of 'ikhtari' and the wife's response specifying 'first, middle, last'. Then identify that Abu Hanifa rules three divorces without need for intention, while the Sahibayn rule one divorce.
The disagreement is purely within the Hanafi school.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's reasoning
The Sahibayn argue that mentioning 'first, middle, last' does not create order in divorce because the right to divorce is not sequential. They acknowledge individualization but deny order, thus only one divorce results.
They focus on the nature of the right (talaq) which is not ordered like a location.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa argues that speech inherently implies order and individualization. The repetition of 'ikhtari' itself indicates multiple delegations. If the repetition were meaningless, it would be null in the original and thus also in the derivative.
He prioritizes the literal implication of speech over the nature of the right.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view. This is based on the strength of his dalil and the acceptance by later scholars like Al-Marghinani.
The practical consequence is that three irrevocable divorces occur in this scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولوقال لها اختارى اختارى اختارى فقالت اخترت الاولى والوسطى والاخيرة طلقت ثلثا في قول ابي حنيفة ولا يحتاج الى نية الزوج وقالا تطلق واحدة وانما لا يحتاج الى نية الزوج لدلالة التكرار عليه اذ الاختيار فى حق الطلاق هو الذى يتكرر لهما ان ذكر الاولى وما يجرى مجراه ان كان لا يفيد من حيث الترتيب و لكن يفيد من حيث الافراد فيعتبر فيما يفيد وله ان هذا وصف لغولانه المجتمع فی الملک لا ترتيب فيه كالمجتمع فى المكان والكلام للترتيب والافراد من ضروراته فاذا لغافي حق الاصل لغا في حق البناء
And if he said to her: 'Ikhtari, ikhtari, ikhtari' (choose, choose, choose) and she said: 'I chose the first, the middle, and the last', she is divorced three times according to Abu Hanifa, and there is no need for the husband's intention. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: She is divorced once. And the reason there is no need for the husband's intention is the indication of repetition. Because choice (ikhtiyar) with respect to divorce is that which is repeated. For them (the Sahibayn), mentioning the first and what is like it does not benefit in terms of order, but it benefits in terms of individualization, so it is considered regarding what it benefits. And for him (Abu Hanifa): This is a description of that which is gathered in ownership; there is no order in it, like that which is gathered in a place. Speech is for order and individualization is a necessity of it. So if it becomes meaningless in the original, it becomes meaningless in the derivative.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the repetition of the word 'ikhtari' three times by the husband, and the wife's response specifying 'the first, the middle, and the last'. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that three divorces occur, and importantly, there is no need to ask the husband about his intention (niyyah) because the repetition itself indicates a desire for multiple divorces. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) rule that only one divorce occurs. Their reasoning is that the wife's mention of 'first, middle, last' does not create order in divorce because the right to divorce is not sequential like items in a place. However, Abu Hanifa argues that speech is for order and individualization, and if the repetition is meaningless in the original (i.e., if no order is intended), it still has effect in the derivative (i.e., each 'ikhtari' is a separate delegation). The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, as it is the basis for practice.

Key Terms
اختیار (ikhtiyar): The option given to the wife to choose; repeated three times.
ترتیب (tartib): Order or sequence. Sahibayn deny order in divorce rights.
افراد (ifrad): Individualization; the wife's response individualizes the choices.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because the right to divorce is not sequential
C) Because the husband did not intend multiple divorces
D) Because the repetition of 'ikhtari' is not evidence

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that three repetitions of 'ikhtari' with an appropriate response by the wife result in three divorces, without needing to inquire into the husband's intention.
