Riding an Animal or Ship and the Wife's Khiyar
Rulings on khiyar when riding animal or ship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on khiyar for a wife riding an animal or ship, and distinguish when movement invalidates the option.

Core Idea
Movement under the wife's control invalidates khiyar; movement beyond her control does not.

When a wife receives the right to divorce herself (amr bi yadik), her physical conduct can indicate whether she is still deliberating or has turned away. This lesson examines how riding an animal versus a ship affects the validity of her khiyar, based on the degree of control she has over the conveyance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
The act is the wife's khiyar (option) after being granted amr bi yadik. The condition affecting it is her movement while riding. Determine whether her movement is under her control.
Movement on an animal is attributed to the rider; movement on a ship is not.
2
Apply the rule to animal riding
If the animal stops, her khiyar remains. If it continues walking, her khiyar is invalidated because the animal's motion is attributed to her and indicates disregard.
The rider can control the animal; continued motion shows lack of deliberation.
3
Apply the rule to ship riding
A ship is like a house: its movement is not attributed to the passenger. Therefore, if the ship moves, her khiyar is not invalidated.
The passenger cannot stop the ship, so movement does not indicate disregard.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on leaning
The text presents two narrations: one from al-Jami' al-Saghir (leaning does not invalidate khiyar) and one from al-Mabsut (leaning does invalidate khiyar). The author prefers al-Jami' al-Saghir's view.
The dispute hinges on whether leaning constitutes turning away (i'rad) or is merely a change of posture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كانت تسير على دابة اوفى محمل فوقفت فهی علی خیارها و ان سارت بطل خيارها لان سير الدابة ووقوفها مضاف اليها والسفينة بمنزلة البيت لان سيرها غير مضاف الى راكبها الاترى انه لا يقدر على ايقافها وراكب الدابة يقدر
اور اگر عورت کسی جانور پر چل رہی تھی یا حمل میں تھی پھر سواری ٹھہری تو یہ اپنے اختیار پر ہوگی۔ اور گر جانور چلتا رہا تو اس کا خیار باطل ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ جانور کا چلنا اور شہر نا عورت ہی کی جانب منسوب ہے اور کشتی بمنزلہ گھر کے ہے۔ کیونکہ کشتی کا چلنا اس کے سوار کی طرف منسوب نہیں کیا نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ سوار کو کشتی ٹھہرانے پر قدرت نہیں ہے۔ اور جانور کا سوار قادر ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ امر بالید کے وقت کھڑی تھی اس کے بعد بیٹھ گئی تو اس کا خیار باقی ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیٹھنا متوجہ ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ کیونکہ بیٹھ کو غور کرنا بہ نسبت کھڑا ہونے کے بہتر ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر وہ بیٹھی تھی پس اختیار ملنے کے بعد تکیہ لگالیا یا تکیہ لگائے ہوئے تھی پھر اختیار کے بعد بیٹھ گئی۔ تو اس صورت میں اس کا اختیار باطل نہیں ہوا بلکہ وہ اپنے اختیار پر باقی ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ ایک حالت سے دوسری حالت کی طرف منتقل ہونا ہے۔ اس کو اعراض اور روگردانی نہیں کہا جا سکتا۔ اور یہا لیا ہے جیسا کہ وہ اختیار ملنے کے وقت دونوں گھٹے کھڑے کیئے بیٹھی تھی ۔ پھر چار زانو ہو کر بیٹھ گئی تو اس کا خیار باطل نہیں ہوا۔ مصنف ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ خیار کا باقی رہنا اس صورت میں ہے، جبکہ بیٹھی تھی پھر تکیہ لگالیا۔ جامع صغیر کی روایت ہے ورنہ جامع صغیر کے علاوہ مبسوط کی روایت یہ ہے کہ اگر امر بالید کے وقت بیٹھی تھی پھر تکیہ لگا لیا تو اس کے لیئے خیار باقی نہیں رہے گا۔ کیونکہ تکیہ لگانا امر بالید کی طرف التفات نہ کرنے کی دلیل ہے۔ پس تکیہ لگانا اعراض شمار ہو گا۔ قول اول یعنی جامع صغیر کی روایت زیادہ صحیح ہے۔
And if she was walking on an animal or in a litter, and then it stopped, she is upon her option; and if it walked, her option is invalidated, because the walking and stopping of the animal are attributed to her. And the ship is like a house, because its movement is not attributed to its rider. Do you not see that the rider cannot stop it, but the rider of an animal can. And if the woman was walking on an animal or in a litter and then the riding stopped, she will be upon her option. And if the animal continued walking, her khiyar became invalid, because the animal's walking and stopping are attributed to the woman. And the ship is like a house, because its movement is not attributed to its rider. Do you not see that the rider has no power to stop it, but the rider of an animal has power. Explanation of the issue: When she was standing at the time of amr bi yadik and then sat down, her khiyar remains. The proof is that sitting is a sign of turning towards, because sitting for contemplation is better than standing. Similarly, if she was sitting and then leaned after receiving the option, or was leaning and then sat after the option, in this case her option is not invalidated; rather she remains upon her option, because this is a transition from one state to another, and it cannot be called turning away or disregard. And like this, if she was sitting with both knees up at the time of the option and then sat cross-legged, her khiyar is not invalidated. The author of Hidayah says that this remaining of khiyar is in the case when she was sitting and then leaned. This is the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir. Otherwise, besides al-Jami' al-Saghir, the narration of al-Mabsut is that if she was sitting at the time of amr bi yadik and then leaned, she will not have khiyar, because leaning is evidence of not paying attention to the matter. So leaning is considered turning away. The first view, i.e., the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir, is more correct.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct rulings. First, regarding a wife who is riding an animal or in a litter (mahmil) when she receives amr bi yadik: if the animal stops, her khiyar remains; if it continues walking, her khiyar is invalidated. The reasoning is that the movement of the animal is attributed to her (since she controls it), so continuing to move indicates she is not pausing to consider the option. However, a ship is like a house because its movement is not under the rider's control; the rider cannot stop it, so movement on a ship does not invalidate the khiyar. The second part repeats and emphasizes the earlier rulings on sitting and leaning, stating that the preferred view (from al-Jami' al-Saghir) is that leaning does not invalidate the option.

Key Terms
دابة (dabbah): A riding animal (horse, camel, etc.)
محمل (mahmil): A litter or howdah carried by an animal.
سفينة (safinah): Ship or boat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a ship treated differently from an animal?
A) Because a ship is larger and more stable.
B) Because the rider cannot stop the ship, so movement is not attributed to her.
C) Because ships are mentioned in the Quran.
D) Because a ship has a captain.

Key Takeaway
The wife's khiyar is invalidated only by actions under her control that indicate disregard; movement in a vehicle she cannot control does not affect it.

Talaq — Divorce

Effect of Posture Changes on a Woman's Option in Divorce
Rulings on khiyar with posture changes and two riwayas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on posture changes during khiyar, identify i'rad as the invalidating factor, and apply the tarjih between two riwayas.

Core Idea
A woman's khiyar is only invalidated by clear i'rad; posture changes alone do not end it, but riding animal movement does.

When a husband gives his wife the right to divorce herself (amr bil yad), her khiyar remains valid until she clearly turns away (i'rad). This passage from al-Hidayah examines borderline scenarios: she stands then sits, sits then leans, lies on her side, seeks consultation, or is riding an animal or boat. The text also presents an intra-Hanafi difference on side-lying, showing how the school resolves conflicting riwayas. Understanding these rulings requires grasping the concept of i'rad and the rational proofs used.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
Understand that the woman's khiyar remains unless she displays i'rad (turning away). Recognize that posture changes alone do not constitute i'rad unless they indicate carelessness.
i'rad is subjective and context-dependent.
2
Apply the principle to each scenario
Work through the scenarios: standing to sitting (option remains), sitting to leaning (disputed but preferred view: remains), lying on side (two riwayas), seeking consultation (remains), riding animal (invalid if animal moves, valid if stops), boat (always remains). For each, identify whether the action indicates attention or i'rad.
The text gives specific rulings based on fatwa.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi difference
For the side-lying case, note the two riwayas from Abu Yusuf. Understand that one riwaya (from Hasan ibn Ziyad) considers it not i'rad, while the other (from Hasan ibn Abi Malik) considers it i'rad. See how the author resolves by stating 'awwal azhar' (first is more correct).
This is a classic example of tarjih between riwayas.
4
Distinguish between animal and boat
Note the key difference: the movement of an animal is attributed to the rider (she can stop it), so moving invalidates her option. But a boat's movement is not attributed to her (she cannot stop it), so it does not invalidate. This is based on rational reasoning (dalil aqli).
The analogy uses the concept of ability to control.

And if she was standing then sat, she is upon her option. Because sitting indicates attention, as sitting collects opinion well. Similarly, if she was sitting then leaned, or was leaning and then sat, because this is a transfer from one state to another, so it is not i'rad. Like when she was sitting with knees upright then sat cross-legged. The author said: this is the riwaya of Jami' al-Saghir. And in other than it, it is mentioned that when she was sitting then leaned, she has no option, because leaning indicates carelessness, so leaning is i'rad. And the first is more correct. And if she was sitting then lay on her side, there are two riwayas from Abu Yusuf. And if she said: 'Let me call my father to consult' or 'call witnesses to testify', she is upon her option, because consultation is to obtain correct opinion and testifying is to avoid denial, so this is not i'rad. And if she was riding an animal or was in a litter and the mount stopped, she is upon her option; if the mount moved, her option is void, because the movement/stopping of the animal is attributed to her. And a ship is like a house, because the ship's movement is not attributed to its rider; do you not see that the rider cannot stop the ship, while the rider of an animal can.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of rulings regarding the woman's khiyar (option) when given the right to divorce herself (amr bil yad). The text discusses how changes in the woman's posture after being given the option affect the validity of her khiyar. The general principle is that minor changes that do not indicate i'rad (turning away from the option) preserve the option, while deliberate actions showing disregard invalidate it. The passage provides specific scenarios: standing to sitting preserves option; sitting to leaning is debated; lying on one's side has two riwayas from Imam Abu Yusuf. Seeking consultation or calling witnesses does not invalidate the option. Regarding transportation, if the woman is riding an animal, her option is valid if the animal stops (since stopping is attributed to her) but invalid if it moves (since she motioned it). For a boat, however, the option remains regardless of movement, because the boat's movement is not attributed to the rider—the rider cannot stop it. The commentary then clarifies each point with reasoning.

Key Terms
خیار (khiyar): The woman's option to choose whether to accept or reject divorce when given the right by her husband.
اعراض (i'rad): Turning away or showing disinterest in the option, which invalidates it.
جامع صغیر (Jami' al-Saghir): One of the six zahir al-riwayah books by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman is given the option to divorce herself while sitting, and then she lies on her side, what is the ruling according to the two riwayas from Abu Yusuf?
A) In both riwayas, her option is invalidated.
B) In one riwaya, option remains; in the other, it is invalidated.
C) Her option remains in both riwayas.
D) The option is invalidated only if she falls asleep.

Key Takeaway
A woman's khiyar is only invalidated by clear i'rad, and the preferred Hanafi view is that leaning and lying on side do not constitute i'rad.

Khiyar on Animal vs Boat: Attribution of Control
Ruling on khiyar validity during movement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on khiyar validity when the wife is on a moving animal versus a boat, and explain the rationale based on attribution of control.

Core Idea
A wife's khiyar is valid on a moving boat but void on a moving animal because she can control the animal but not the boat.

This passage from the Hidayah presents a nuanced ruling about the khiyar (option) given to a wife in talaq. It distinguishes between two modes of transport—animal and boat—based on the wife's ability to control the movement. Understanding this distinction requires grasping the Hanafi principle of attribution (isnad) and customary capability. The ruling is based on rational reasoning (dalil aqli) rooted in the reality of control.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling for each case
Read the passage and note the two scenarios: wife on an animal vs wife on a boat. For each, determine whether the khiyar remains valid or becomes void after the option is given.
The passage clearly states the outcome for each.
2
Explain the rationale for the animal case
The movement of the animal is attributed to the rider because she can control it (by stopping or dismounting). If she does not stop it, her inaction is considered a rejection of the option, voiding the khiyar.
Key term: mansub (attributed).
3
Explain the rationale for the boat case
The movement of the boat is not attributed to the rider because she cannot control it. Therefore, the khiyar remains valid regardless of movement.
Boat is compared to a house – the rider has no ability to stop it.
4
Contrast the two cases to extract the principle
The underlying principle is attribution of movement to the wife when she has the ability to control it. If she has control but does not exercise it, the movement is considered her choice, which nullifies the option. If she lacks control, the movement does not affect the option.
This is a rational (aqli) ruling based on custom and capability.
5
Apply the principle to a modern equivalent
Consider a car vs a train. A wife in a car can stop it (like an animal), so if she continues moving, the khiyar is void. A wife on a train cannot stop it (like a boat), so the khiyar remains valid. This extends the principle analogically.
This step reinforces the reasoning beyond the text.

اور اگر وہ عورت جانور پر رواں تھی یا عمل میں تھی اس وقت شوہر نے اختیار دیا پھر سواری ٹھہر گئی تو یہ عورت اپنے اختیار پر باقی ہے اور اگر وہ جانور چل دیا تو اس کا خیار باطل ہو جائے گا کیونکہ جانور کا چلنا اور اس کا ٹھہر ناعورت کی جانب منسوب ہوگا ۔ اور کشتی بمنزلہ گھر کے ہے۔ یعنی اگر کشتی چلتی رہی تو اس عورت کا خیار باطل نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کشتی کا چلنا اسکے سوار کی طرف منسوب نہیں ہوگا۔ چنانچہ آپ غور کیجئے کر کشتی کا سوار کشتی کو ٹھہرانے پر قادر نہیں ، البتہ جانور کا سوار اس کو ٹھہرانے پر قادر ہے۔
And if that woman was mounted on an animal or was in the act (of riding) when the husband gave her the option (ikhtiyar), then the mount stopped, then this woman remains with her option. And if the animal moved, then her khiyar will become void because the movement of the animal and its stopping are attributed to the woman. And a boat is like a house. That is, if the boat continued moving, then the woman's khiyar does not become void because the movement of the boat is not attributed to its rider. So reflect that the rider of a boat is not able to stop it, whereas the rider of an animal is able to stop it.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hidayah about khiyar (option) when the wife is given the authority (takhyeer) by the husband during a state of movement. The ruling distinguishes between riding on an animal and riding in a boat. The key principle is attribution: when the wife is on an animal, she can control its stopping, so her failure to stop it is attributed to her, nullifying the option. But on a boat, she cannot control the movement, so her option remains regardless of motion. This is a rational (aqli) ruling based on customary understanding of control.

Key Terms
اختیار (ikhtiyar): The option or authority given by the husband to the wife to divorce herself.
خیار (khiyar): The right or option that the wife possesses after being given the authority.
رواں (rawan): Moving or in motion, used here for the animal or boat.
منسوب (mansub): Attributed or ascribed; the movement is considered to be under the control of the rider.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a husband gives his wife the option while she is riding a boat that continues moving?
A) Her khiyar becomes void because the boat is moving.
B) Her khiyar remains valid because she cannot control the boat.
C) Her khiyar becomes void only if she stands up.
D) Her khiyar remains valid only if the boat is anchored.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a wife's khiyar depends on whether she has control over the movement; if she can but does not stop, the option is void.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Rulings on Husband Saying 'Talliqi Nafsik' to His Wife
Ruling on divorce delegation with various intentions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that 'talaq' is an ism jins to determine the number of divorces when a husband delegates divorce to his wife.

Core Idea
Talaq is a generic noun – it defaults to one but accepts intention for three, not two.

When a husband commands his wife 'talliqi nafsik' (divorce yourself), the legal effect depends on both parties' intentions. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi view on how the generic nature of the word 'talaq' determines the outcome, including why intending three works but intending two does not (except for a slave woman).

Guided Path
1
Identify the delegation and initial conditions
Note the husband's phrase is a command: 'talliqi nafsik'. The default is no specific intention or only one.
The wife's response 'tallaqtu nafsi' completes the divorce action.
2
Understand 'talaq' as an ism jins
Recognize that 'talaq' is a generic noun (ism jins) that primarily denotes the smallest unit (one divorce) but can encompass the entire class (three divorces) by intention.
This principle is central to the ruling.
3
Apply intention rules
If the husband intends three, it is effective; if no intention, one revocable divorce occurs. Intention for two is invalid because two is a specific number, not a jins.
The exception is for a slave woman, where two is considered the jins.
4
Derive the final ruling
Combine the conditions and intention: the divorce is revocable because the delegated power is for a clear (sarih) divorce.
This ruling is the mufta bihi Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في المشية
ترجمه فصل مشیت کے ( بیان) میں ہے
عورت کو طلقی نفسک کہا کوئی نیت نہیں تھی یا ایک کی نیت کی تھی تو عورت نے طلقت نفسی کہا تو ایک طلاق رجعی واقع ہو جائے گی

ومن قال لامراة طلقی نفسك ولانية له اونوى واحدة فقالت طلقت نفسى فهى واحدة رجعية وان طلقت نفسها ثلثا وقدار اد الزوج ذلك وقعن عليها وهذا لان قوله طلقی معناه افعلى فعل الطلاق وهو اسم جنس فيقع على الادنى مع احتمال الكل كسائر اسماء الاجناس فلهذا تعمل فيه نية الثلث وينصرف الى واحدة عند عدمها وتكون الواحدة رجعية لان المفوض اليها صريح الطلاق وهو رجعى ولونوى الثنتين لا يصح لانه نية العدد الا اذا كانت المنكوحة امة لانه جنس في حقها

ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے اپنی عورت سے کہا تو اپنے آپ کو طلاق دے۔ اور شوہر کی کوئی نیت نہیں یا اس نے ایک کی نیت کی ہے۔ پس عورت نے کہا میں نے اپنے آپکو طلاق دی تو یہ ایک رجعی ہوگی۔ اور اگر اس نے اپنے آپ کو تین دی حالانکہ شوہر نے اس کا ارادہ بھی کیا ہے تو اس پر ( تینوں ) واقع ہو جائیں گی اور یہ اسلئے ہے کہ اس کا قول طلقی اسکے معنی ہیں کہ طلاق کا فعل کر تو اور طلاق اسم جنس ہے۔ پس لفظ طلاق واقع ہوگا ادنی (ایک) پر کل (تین ) کے احتمال کے ساتھ جیسا کہ تمام اسماء اجناس ۔ پس اسی وجہ سے طلاق میں تین کی نیست کارآمد ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور عدم نیت کے وقت ایک کی طرف راجح ہوگی۔ اور ایک رجعی ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ عورت کی طرف جو سپرد کی گئی ہے صریح الطلاق ہے اور وہ رجعی ہے۔ اور اگر دو کی نیت کی تو صحیح نہیں ۔ اسلئے کہ یہ نیت عدد ہے مگر جبکہ منکوحہ باندی ہو ، کیونکہ وہ اسکے حق میں جنس ہے۔

تشریح مسئلہ، اگر مرد نے اپنی منکوحہ سے طلقی نفسک کہا اور مرد نے کوئی نیت نہیں کی یا ایک طلاق کی نیت کی ہے۔ پھر عورت نے جواب میں طلقت نفسی کہا تو ایک رجعی واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اگر عورت نے اپنے اوپر تین واقع کیسں درانحالیکہ شوہر نے تین کی نیت بھی کی ہے تو عورت پر تین واقع ہو جائیں گی۔ ان دونوں صورتوں کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ طلقی کے معنی ہیں افعلی فعل الطلاق یعنی صیغہ امر صدر كو ہے۔ اور مصدر اسم جنس ہے۔ اور اسم جنس اونی یعنی فرد حقیقی پر صادق آتا ہے۔ کل جنس یعنی فرد کمی کے احتمال کے ساتھ ۔ یہی حکم تمام اسماء اجناس کا ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ طلقی میں تین کی نیت کرنا صحیح ہے۔ اور اگر نیت نہیں کی ہے تو فرد حقیقی (ایک) کی طرف راجح ہوگا۔ اور یہ ایک رجعی ہوگی ۔ اسکی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت کے سپر دھریح الطلاق ہے اور صریح الطلاق سے طلاق رجعی واقع ہوتی ہے۔

اور اگر دو کی نیت کی تو صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ دو عدد ہے اور مصدر سے عدد کی نیت درست نہیں ہوتی۔ البتہ اگر منکوحہ باندی ہو تو پھر دو کی نیت بھی صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ دو باندی کے حق میں جنس یعنی فرد دکھی ہے۔
Chapter on the Conditional. Translation: The chapter on the conditional (mashiyyah) is about. If the husband said to his wife 'talliqi nafsik' (divorce yourself) and had no intention or intended one, and the wife said 'tallaqtu nafsi' (I divorced myself), then one revocable divorce occurs. And whoever said to his wife 'talliqi nafsik' with no intention or one intention, and she said 'tallaqtu nafsi', then it is one revocable. And if she divorced herself three times and the husband intended that, they fall upon her. This is because his saying 'talliqi' means 'perform the action of talaq', and talaq is a generic noun (ism jins), so it applies to the minimum with the possibility of all, like other generic nouns. Thus intention for three is effective, and it defaults to one when there is no intention. The one is revocable because what is delegated to her is clear divorce (sarih talaq), which is revocable. If he intended two, it is not valid, because it is intention for a number, unless the wife is a slave, because two is a jins for her. (Then Urdu translation and commentary follow, essentially repeating the same meanings.) Clarification of the issue: ... And if he intended two, it is not valid, because two is a number and intention for a number from a masdar is not valid. However, if the wife is a slave, then intention for two is valid, because two for her is the jins, i.e., the minimal individual.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Hidayah about the delegation of divorce when the husband commands 'talliqi nafsik'. The key analysis is that 'tallaq' is an ism jins (generic noun), meaning it primarily denotes the smallest individual (one divorce) but can encompass all individuals (three divorces) by intention. Therefore, if the husband intends three, it is effective; if no intention, it defaults to one. Intention for two is invalid for a free woman because two is a specific number, not a jins, but for a slave woman, two is the maximum, so it is considered the jins. The resulting divorce is revocable because the delegated power is for a clear (sarih) divorce. This is the established Hanafi position.

Key Terms
طلق (tallaq): Divorce; here used as a verbal noun (masdar) meaning the act of divorcing.
اسم جنس (ism jins): A generic noun that applies to the smallest unit (fard haqiqi) while allowing for the entire class by intention.
رجعی (raj'i): Revocable divorce, meaning the husband may take back the wife without a new marriage during the waiting period.
نیت عدد (niyyat al-adad): Intention for a specific number (e.g., two divorces), which is invalid because the masdar does not convey number.
باندی (bandi): Slave woman; for her, two is considered the jins because it is the maximum number of divorces applicable to a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his free wife 'talliqi nafsik' and intends two divorces, and she responds 'tallaqtu nafsi', what is the ruling?
A) Two revocable divorces occur.
B) One revocable divorce occurs.
C) No divorce occurs.
D) Two divorces occur, but one is revocable.

Key Takeaway
Talaq as an ism jins defaults to one revocable divorce but can be increased to three by intention; two is invalid for free women but valid for slaves.
